Pro-Tint is local and decided to give them business because they know what they're doing. If you live in SoCal, tinted windows are a must. The nonstop heat we receive each year is ridiculous and if your car has leather seats, tinted windows will prolong the life of those seats from harmful UV rays. Unlike some other businesses are first come first serve, they accept appointments and will give you a reasonable time frame.

One caveat that I should mention is that when I took the two cars to get windows tinted during Covid and the employees here had their masks off or wearing them on their chins while installing tint on cars. When entering the business, the lady at the front desk (Jasmine) didn't wear hers either until someone (me) walked into the building. Even before vaccines were offered, I saw it on both occasions (dropping off and picking up) that masks were not worn properly, either not wearing it on wearing it on their chins. I assume they don't want to wear it or hinders them while working on the cars but I honestly believe the owner should make it a priority that his/her employees are safe and following protocols. All I can do is make note of everything since it's their decision not to do it.

If you  plan on getting your tint here, I do recommend sanitizing everything in your car just to be safe. Also, when I picked up my Subaru and Toyota, there was a small piece of a blue towel was was stuck by the front windshield and the windshield pillar. There was also trash that was left behind by the passenger door. I don't mind throwing it away but I wished they looked carefully that nothing was left. If they give you a pickup window time of 2-3 hours, it may be longer. I dropped off my car at 12:15 for a 12:30 appointment, was given a 3-3:30 pickup time. Jasmine called me at 5:00 asking if anyone called me to pick it up, which no one did. They she told me that it's ready for pickup. So there are small things that irked me, which is why I gave this place 3 stars. However, this business still did what they're known for and I'm thankful it turned out great. I just recommend some improvements internally.

To give you an idea of how much you might pay, when I first brought my Subaru Outback here May 2020, I got my front windshield tint (3M Crystalline) for $250. Couple months later, I had to remove it because Subaru of American needed me to remove it in order to fix an issue with my vehicle. I came back couple days ago to get the same exact tint installed on my front windshield, yet they charged me $329 (including tax). I have no idea why the price increased for the past 11 months for the same windshield. The rest of my windows for my Subaru was $733 (including tax) for 3M Color Stable. For the Prius Prime, It was $318 for all windows, using 3M Color Stable.<//Review>

<user_name>Shelley P.<//user_name>< Review>
My only regret is not having enough stomach space to get literally everything in this whole bakery. I think takeout dimsum/Chinese bakeries are my favorite part of the food scene in San Francisco.

We came here actually because Golden Gate Bakery wasn't open yet/didn't have egg tarts that day and I'm not sad about it at all! My friend and I got shrimp and chive dumplings, potstickers, custard buns, egg tarts, sachima, and a zhongzhi all for about $11! The dumplings weren't warm (but still really good and homey), but the egg tarts were FRESH out of the oven, literally steaming, the crusts were so flaky and buttery and the custard was melt-in-your-mouth heavenly. What's Golden Gate?! The sachima - which I've never had a fresh one before - was a bit too oily but I also baseline am just obsessed with sachima so I was still loving it.

Also - they take card WHOOHOO<//Review>

< Review>
This place always has fresh and good-sized dim sums with the line moving quickly.  They have all the regulars such as shrimp dumpling, sui Chinese  tamale, but their unexpected winners are their desserts - their mochis (glutinous rice balls with red bean paste or peanuts) are out of this world and are only $1.80 for three, and their egg tarts and sesame ball are good, too.  The best thing is that their desserts and dim sums are probably the cheapest around Chinatown. If you like a hot Hong Kong style milk tea- theirs is pretty good too!< /Review>

< text>
Was drawn to this bakery by the queue snaking out the door and boy, am I glad i did.

Got the sesame balls with red bean filling (3x for $1.80) - light, airy with a good dough to filling ratio, the sesame seeds also added a nice fragrance and the fresh prawn rice rolls (~$1.90) - would have loved to see more prawns but at this price I cannot complain, best eaten drowned in the accompanying soya sauce.

Prices are real wallet friendly, makes a great meal but the lack of space in the shop means that it‚Äôs to-go only, unless you‚Äôre lucky enough to snag the only table in the shop.</text>

<Review>Like most places in Chinatown, people don't speak fluent English, but all you have to do is point and say how many.  Also many of the signs are in Chinese, so you can point and ask how much.  It's ok, I do it all the time and they're more than happy to help out.  So now you know how I order here, I point, say one order this, point one order that.  Just make sure they know what you're pointing at.

This place is a cheap take out dim sum place.  I always get the fried stuff here, there's a savory dish I like that is cooked pork in a mochi wrapper that is deep fried, both sweet and savory.  I think it's 3 for $1.60,  they package it in a plastic bag (most places do this), which actually makes it less messy to eat because you can just use the bag to grasp it.  The best deal is the milk tea with bobba.  They have milk or coffee flavor for $.99, while other places are $1.99 and up.  They make theirs stronger, but it's pretty sweet.

I go here and get a couple of things and can get filled up on 5 bucks.< /Review><response>None<//response>< user>

Give this course a try! The front 9 will lead you to believe it's on the flat side.Tee to green that is , now the greens are sneaky sloped. Just when you feel this is sinking the hole , reality check hits you.The greens are a challenge with the gentle yet ball commanding lines. Overall wide open. Don't  at anytime take your eye off the ball. The ball will vanish on you with going into the neighboring properties. And the staff was very hospitable and the service is great! <user>103155854192902751675<//user><name>Bryan P</name><Time>1433821423363< /Time><Rating>1<//Rating>< Review>
Its horrible. The people aren't very happy to help at all, they give you a rude look when you ask for something, and not at all welcoming. A few years ago they took away the magazine seating area, took away chairs, and patched up all the wall plugs to make sure nobody charges their phones or laptops. Barnes and Noble doesn't even give coupons. Its why competition is so important.

Borders always welcomed customers with friendly service, constantly gave 40% off coupons every week, and never acted as selfish as B&N has. I just get everything from Amazon now or go to the library nearby.

Highly recommend the Montclair mall B&N, they have more in stock, starbucks seating area, more inventory and they aren't greedy with letting people relax and read a book. Well worth the extra drive.</Review>

< Review>
I thought one of the few advantages of brick-and-mortar bookstores was the welcoming environment and the ability to go there and study or quietly hang out for a little while. Not so at this store. The employees are not that friendly, there are no tables, there are few chairs and the ones there are are bolted to the wall, and although there is very mediocre wifi, they get upset if you plug in and with nowhere to sit and put your laptop or books there's no point in it anyway.

I generally make it a point to buy from any store that has wifi and is gracious about allowing me to use it, but due to the unwelcoming staff and environment, I put the books I was going to buy back on the shelves and left to go to the library.<//Review>
